Eggeling
  1. Praj─Бpati created the (Soma-)sacrifice. He took it and performed it. When he had performed it, he felt like one emptied out. He saw this sacrificial performance, the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л, and performed it, and then he was again replenished; and, indeed, he who performs the Soma-sacrifice is, as it were, emptied out, for his wealth, his prosperity is, as it were, taken from him.

Eggeling
  1. Having performed a Soma-sacrifice one ought to perform the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л: as a cow that has been milked would replenish again, even so, indeed, does he replenish himself,–he replenishes himself by offspring and cattle; and, verily, he who, knowing this, performs the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л, or he who (even) knows this, establishes himself in this world, and wins the heavenly world.

  1. Therefore at this sacrifice (the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л) the fast-observance 3 is the initiation. Now, the fast-observance is a male, and the initiation a female; and the truth is a male, and faith a female; and the mind is a male, and speech a female; and the Sacrificer is the male to his wife, whence wherever there is a husband there is a wife: and at the very outset of the sacrifice he thus sets up couples with a view to production.

Eggeling
  1. All (the praishas) contain (the word) ‘payas’ (milk), for in the form of milk Soma is (here) pressed 14; they all contain (the word) ‘Soma,’ for the sake of (conformity with) the Soma-pressing; they all contain (the word) ‘parisrut’ (spirituous liquor), for in the form of spirituous liquor Soma is (here) pressed; they all contain (the word) ‘ghr╠еta’ (ghee), for this–to wit, ghee–doubtless is manifestly a form of the sacrifice: he thus makes it to be manifestly a form of the sacrifice; they all contain (the word) ‘madhu’ (honey), for this–to wit, honey–is manifestly a form of Soma: he thus makes it to be manifestly a form of Soma.

Eggeling
  1. The ─А┼Ыvina cup, indeed, is the eye, the S─Бrasvata one the vital air, and the Aindra one

speech. From the ─А┼Ыvina (cup) he pours (the remains) into the S─Бrasvata one, whereby he combines his eye with the vital airs; from the S─Бrasvata cup) into the Aindra one, whereby he combines his vital airs with his speech, and also establishes his vital airs in (the channel of) speech, whence all the vital airs are established on speech.

  1. Three (men) drink the ─А┼Ыvina (cup), to wit, the Adhvaryu, Pratiprasth─Бtr╠е, and Agn─лdh; for this eye is threefold–the white, the black, and the pupil: he thus bestows on him the eye in accordance with its form.

Eggeling
  1. The invitatory and offering formulas are made continuous, and relate to the same deities–

for the sake of the continuity and uninterruptedness of the seasons. They are all of them invitatory-formulas and all offering-formulas 26, whence all the seasons pass onwards, and all of them return. All (the formulas) are first, all of them intermediate, and all of them last, whence all the seasons are first, all of them intermediate, and all of them last. All the cups have two (formulas, an) invitatory and (an) offering-formula,–this is of the form of day and night: it is the day and the night he thus secures for himself; whence both the seasons and the months are established on day and night.

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╣рд░рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ рдХреГрддреМ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдВрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реЗ рдХрд╛рдВрдбреЗ рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрдореЗ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее резреи ред рео ред реи рее

Eggeling
  1. The Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л, truly, is the same as the year, and the same as the moon; and the Sacrificer is manifestly the sun: his vedi (altar-ground) is this earth, his uttara-vedi the air, his barhis the sky, his officiating priests the quarters, his fuel the trees, his ghee the waters, his oblations the plants, his fire Agni himself, his saс╣Бsth─Б (the particular form of sacrifice) the year–and, indeed, everything here, whatever there is, is the year; whence he who has performed the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л wins everything, and secures everything for himself.

  1. 239:2 Cf. II, 4, 4, 3-4, where the latter is called Prat─лdar┼Ыa ┼Ъvaikna (king of the ┼Ъvikna), whilst the former, after studying with him, is said to have been called Sahadeva S─Бr├▒jaya. ↩︎

  2. 240:1 The ‘Som─Бс╣Б┼Ыava iva’ would seem to have here the force of ‘Soma-shoots proper,’ only substitutes (milk and liquor) being used instead. ↩︎

  3. 240:2 That is to say, the observance of the fast–by which the Sacrificer during the four days of the performance of the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л, lives solely on the remains of the Agnihotra–takes the place of the ordinary initiation of the Soma-sacrifice, there being no D─лksh─Б at the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л. ↩︎

  5. 240:3 The malted rice, malted barley, and fried rice, referred to in this and the next two paragraphs, refer to the remnants of these materials, not used at first in the preparation of the Sur─Б, and amounting to one-third of the original quantity of each; these being added successively during the three nights during which the Sur─Б has to mature; cf. p. 223, note 2. ↩︎

  6. 241:1 Or, he renders him, the Sacrificer (or, perhaps, it, the sacrifice), successful by means of the morning-pressing. ↩︎

  7. 241:2 The literal translation would seem to be,–he thus provides him with the respective (sva) world, with the respective deity, and with the respective form,–(hence) with the morning-pressing. It may be remarked, however, that the deities here connected with the three services (the A┼Ыvins, Sarasvat─л, and Indra) are not those elsewhere associated with them (Vasus, Rudras, and ─Аdityas, IV, 3, 5, 1; or Agni, Indra, Vi┼Ыve Dev─Бс╕е, XI, 5, 9, 7). ↩︎

  8. 241:3 Viz. inasmuch as it is full of moisture (saras). ↩︎

  9. 242:1 The ’enam’ must refer to the Sur─Б-liquor, treated as identical with Soma. ↩︎

  10. 242:2 I do not quite understand the distinction between suta’ and ‘─Бsuta ‘; cf. XII, 8, 1, 6; unless the former be the pure Soma-juice, and the latter that mixed with other ingredients. ↩︎

  13. 242:3 The ‘praisha’ are the directions by which the Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зa calls on the Hotr╠е to recite the offering-formulas (cf. part ii, p. 183, note 2). For the fore-offerings of the three victims, these directions are given, V─Бj. S. XXI, 29-40. They all commence with ‘Hot─Б yakshat’ (may the Hotr╠е worship!), and end with ‘payaс╕е somaс╕е parisrut─Б ghr╠еtaс╣Б madhu vyantv ─Бjyasya hotar yaja’ (milk, Soma, with parisrut-liquor, ghee, honey,–may they partake of the butter, Hotr╠е worship!). ↩︎

  14. 243:1 ? Literally, ‘by (way of) milk’–or, perhaps, ‘by the admixture of milk–Soma is (here, as it were) produced.’ ↩︎

  19. 244:1 This refers to the puronuv─Бky─Бs and y─Бjy─Бs of the oblations of omentum (vap─Б) of the three victims. For these formulas the three verses, V─Бj. S. XX, 67-69, are used in such a way that verse 1 forms the anuv─Бky─Б, and verse 2 the y─Бjy─Б, of the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ oblation; verse 2 the anuv─Бky─Б, and verse 3 the y─Бjy─Б, of Sarasvat─л’s oblation; and verse 3 the anuv─Бky─Б, and verse 1 the y─Бjy─Б, of Indra’s oblation. In each of the three verses all the three deities are mentioned.–In exactly the same way the three verses, XX, 70-72, are used as the anuv─Бky─Бs and y─Бjy─Бs of the three pa┼Ыupuroс╕Н─Б┼Ыas; and 73-75 as those of the chief oblations (havis) of meat-portions. ↩︎

  22. 244:2 The ─Аpr─лs (propitiatory verses, cf. part ii, p. 185) are the offering-formulas (y─Бjy─Б) of the eleven (or twelve) fore-offerings (pray─Бja) of the animal sacrifice.
